This dynamic adjustment capability gives DyS\x02nakeConv a significant advantage in capturing subtle\r\nchanges in complex scenes.\r\nâ€¢ Pointwise Convolution\r\nPointwise convolution (1Ã—1Ã—3 convolution) [20]linearly\r\ncombines the outputs processed by depthwise convolution', 'EagleEye: An Efficient Flaws Detection Model For\r\nOffshore Wind Turbine Blade\r\nAnonymous\r\nAbstractâ€”Offshore wind turbines are subjected to harsh\r\nmarine environments, including salt mist and storms, which\r\nexacerbate blade wear and damage. As a result, approximately\r\n30% of offshore wind turbines experience varying degrees of\r\nblade damage within the first five years of operation, leading to an\r\nenergy output loss of about 15%. To address this issue, this paper\r\nproposes a detection model called EagleEye. The model enhances\r\ndetection efficiency through the integration of feature extraction\r\nand fusion techniques, along with an optimized inference network\r\narchitecture. Experimental results demonstrate that the EagleEye\r\nmodel achieves an average accuracy of 53.41%, marking a 7.81\r\npercentage point improvement over the baseline modelâ€™s accuracy\r\nof 45.6%. Additionally, EagleEye operates at 14.5 GFLOPs,', '(Regions with CNN features), Fast R-CNN, and Faster R\x02CNN. These algorithms improve detection efficiency through\r\nRegion Proposal Networks (RPN) and significantly enhance\r\nboth accuracy and speed.\r\nThe YOLO (You Only Look Once) series of algorithms rep\x02resents a significant advancement in object detection. YOLO\r\ntransforms object detection into a regression problem, directly\r\npredicting the location and class of objects from images.\r\nIts core advantage lies in the unified and efficient detection\r\nprocess. YOLOv1 detects objects by dividing images into\r\ngrids. Although it is fast, its precision is lacking. YOLOv2\r\nintroduces techniques such as batch normalization and residual\r\nconnections, while YOLOv3 improves small object recog\x02nition by detecting at multiple scales. YOLOv4 further re\x02fines the network structure by introducing CSPDarknet53 as\r\nthe backbone network and PANet among other technologies,\r\nachieving a balance between speed and accuracy. 'models. Experimental results reveal that EagleEye surpasses\r\nthe YOLOv8 baseline and other comparative models, with an\r\naverage precision of 53.41% and a recall rate of 46.39%.\r\nAlthough its GFLOPs measure at 14.5ms, which is slightly\r\nhigher than YOLOv8 with CrossDySnakeConv but lower than\r\nYOLOv8 with FasterNet, the model maintains competitive in\x02ference speed while delivering enhanced detection capabilities.\r\nThe CrossDySnakeConv module enhances multi-scale feature\r\ncapture, improving defect detection, while FasterNet optimizes\r\nfeature extraction, boosting overall efficiency. Thus, EagleEye\r\neffectively balances detection accuracy and computational ef\x02ficiency, demonstrating its potential for practical wind turbine\r\nblade inspections. Future work will focus on expanding the\r\ndataset to cover more defect scenarios and further optimizing\r\nthe model for improved robustness and real-time performance.\r\nREFERENCES\r\n[1] J. 'model achieves an average accuracy of 53.41%, marking a 7.81\r\npercentage point improvement over the baseline modelâ€™s accuracy\r\nof 45.6%. Additionally, EagleEye operates at 14.5 GFLOPs,\r\nwhich represents a 20.3% improvement in computational effi\x02ciency compared to the baseline 18.2 GFLOPs.\r\nI. INTRODUCTION\r\nOffshore wind turbines are increasingly valued for their\r\nstable wind speeds and high utilization, positioning them as a\r\nsignificant source of clean energy. However, these turbinesâ€™\r\nblades are frequently subjected to environmental damage,\r\nsuch as cracks and scratches. Research indicates that blade\r\ndamage can lead to a reduction in turbine power output\r\nby approximately 15% [1]. Traditional manual inspection\r\nmethods are inefficient and less accurate, often failing to\r\ndetect damage early, which adversely impacts the operational\r\nefficiency and safety of wind turbines [2]. 'multi-layer structure of BottleneckDySnakeConv. This module\r\ncaptures multi-level features from input data and fuses features\r\nFig. 5. Pointwise Convolution Structure\r\nat different levels, improving the modelâ€™s performance in\r\ncomplex scenarios. By combining the dynamic characteristics\r\nof DySnakeConv, the efficient spatial feature extraction of\r\ndepthwise convolution, and the cross-channel feature fusion\r\nof pointwise convolution, the CrossDySnakeConv module\r\ndemonstrates outstanding performance in handling complex\r\nscenes.\r\nIV. EXPERIMENTAL PREPARATION AND RESULTS\r\nA. Experimental Environment\r\nTo assess the effectiveness of the proposed method, an\r\nexperimental platform was established with Windows 11 as\r\nthe operating system and PyTorch 12.1 as the deep learning\r\nframework. YOLOv8n was employed as the baseline network\r\nmodel for comparative analysis. The hardware configuration of\r\nthe experimental environment includes an Intel Core i7 CPU,', 'æ ‡é¢˜: èƒ½è§åº¦ä¸¨åˆ†å¸ƒå¼èƒ½æºè¿æ¥å‘å±•è‰¯æœº\né“¾æ¥: http://www.nea.gov.cn/2024-03/15/c_1310767760.htm\næ—¥æœŸ: 2024-03-15', 'defect scenarios and exploring further optimizations for the\r\nEagleEye model.\r\nII. PRELIMINARIES\r\nObject detection is a significant problem in the field of\r\ncomputer vision, aimed at identifying and locating objects of\r\ninterest within images. Traditional object detection methods\r\nmainly involve two stages: feature extraction and object clas\x02sification/localization. Early algorithms, such as Haar features\r\nand HOG (Histogram of Oriented Gradients) combined with\r\nclassifiers (e.g., SVM), relied on hand-crafted features, which\r\nresulted in longer computation times and higher complexity.\r\nWith the advancement of deep learning, detection algorithms\r\nbased on convolutional neural networks (CNNs) have grad\x02ually replaced these traditional methods, such as R-CNN\r\n(Regions with CNN features), Fast R-CNN, and Faster R\x02CNN. These algorithms improve detection efficiency through\r\nRegion Proposal Networks (RPN) and significantly enhance\r\nboth accuracy and speed.', 'æ ‡é¢˜: ç¢³å¸‚åœºå»ºè®¾åŠ©åŠ›ç»¿è‰²å‘å±•\né“¾æ¥: FasterNet Structure\r\nâ€¢ FasterNet Block:\r\nThe functionality of the FasterNet Block [21] includes\r\nfeature extraction and fusion, as well as memory and\r\ncomputation optimization. Through convolution opera\x02tions, the FasterNet Block is capable of extracting both\r\nlocal and global features of images, and it integrates\r\ndifferent levels of features via residual connections. In\r\nthe final two stages, more FasterNet Blocks are placed\r\nto reduce memory access and enhance computational\r\nefficiency. FPS (Frames Per Second)\r\nmeasures the detection speed of the model by counting the\r\nnumber of frames processed per second. mAP (mean Average\r\nPrecision) evaluates the accuracy of the model, calculated\r\nusing Equation (4). The F1 score, which is the harmonic mean\r\nof precision and recall, measures the overall performance and\r\nstability of the model. The formula for the F1 score is provided\r\nin Equation (5).\r\nmAP =\r\n1\r\nn\r\nXn\r\ni=1\r\nAPi, (4)\r\nwhere APiis the average precision for class i and n is\r\nthe number of classes. A higher mAP score indicates better\r\nperformance in detecting multiple classes of defects.\r\nF1 = 2 Ã—\r\nPrecision Ã— Recall\r\nPrecision + Recall\r\n, (5)\r\nwhere Equation (6)\r\nPrecision =\r\nTrue Positives\r\nTrue Positives + False Positives\r\n, (6)\r\nand Equation (7)\r\nRecall =\r\nTrue Positives\r\nTrue Positives + False Negatives\r\n. (7)\r\n.\r\nA higher F1 score indicates a balanced performance be\x02tween precision and recall.', 'key improvements include:\r\n(1) the integration of the FasterNet architecture to reduce\r\ncomputational complexity. By optimizing the backbone of\r\nthe model, real-time processing capabilities are improved.\r\nAdditionally,\r\n(2) the CrossDySnakeConv module is introduced to enhance\r\ndetection accuracy in complex backgrounds and across differ\x02ent target scales. This module combines various convolutional\r\ntechniques to improve feature extraction and fusion capabili\x02ties.\r\n(3)Experimental results indicate that EagleEye surpasses\r\nexisting models in both detection accuracy and inference\r\nspeed, achieving an average precision of 53.41% and 14.5\r\nGFLOPs (billion floating-point operations per second). This\r\nrepresents a significant advancement over baseline models and\r\nother comparative models. The results demonstrate that Eagle\x02Eye provides superior accuracy and real-time performance in\r\ndetecting wind turbine blade damage, effectively addressing a\r\nrange of damage types and complex backgrounds.', 'environments. Overall, the choice of module should be guided\r\nby the specific requirements of the application, balancing the\r\nneed for detection accuracy and computational efficiency.\r\nD. Ablation Experiment\r\nTable 5 shows the performance comparison results of dif\x02ferent models on a specific task. We conducted a series\r\nof ablation experiments on the YOLO V8 model and its\r\nvariants to evaluate the impact of various components on\r\nmodel performance. Specifically, we compared the baseline\r\nYOLO V8 model, variants incorporating CrossDySnakeConv\r\nand FasterNet, and our model EagleEye in terms of accuracy,', 'DySnakeConv modules, known for their dynamic adjustments,\r\nalso enhance accuracy. CONCLUSIONS\r\nIn this study, we introduced EagleEye, a novel multi-target\r\ndefect detection model that leverages advanced technologies to\r\nsignificantly enhance both accuracy and efficiency in detecting\r\ndefects on wind turbine blades, such as black spots, cracks,\r\nscratches, and coating damage. By integrating the CrossDyS\x02nakeConv module with the FasterNet architecture, EagleEye\r\nachieves superior detection performance compared to existing\r\nmodels. Experimental results reveal that EagleEye surpasses\r\nthe YOLOv8 baseline and other comparative models, with an\r\naverage precision of 53.41% and a recall rate of 46.39%.', 'meaningful features. EAGLEEYE MODEL DESIGN\r\nIn response to the challenges of detecting complex defects in\r\noffshore wind turbine blades, specifically capturing multi-scale\r\nfeatures, detecting small and subtle defects, and meeting real\x02time processing demands under constrained computational\r\nresources, we propose an enhanced YOLOv8 model named\r\nEagleEye. This model incorporates several advancements, as\r\nshown in Figure 1, including\r\n(1) the optimization of real-time processing capabilities\r\nthrough the accelerated inference network architecture, Faster\x02Net [19]\r\n(2) the improvement of multi-scale feature extraction and\r\nfusion mechanisms via the design and application of the\r\nCrossDySnakeConv module.\r\nThe details of these improvements are as follows:\r\nFig. 1. 'changes in complex scenes.\r\nâ€¢ Pointwise Convolution\r\nPointwise convolution (1Ã—1Ã—3 convolution) [20]linearly\r\ncombines the outputs processed by depthwise convolution\r\nand DySnakeConv, achieving cross-channel information\r\nfusion. By fusing all channels at each pixel, pointwise\r\nconvolution enhances feature richness and the modelâ€™s\r\nnon-linear capability as shown Figure 5.\r\nFinally, pointwise convolution integrates all features, pro\x02ducing the final output feature map. This step not only\r\nconsolidates previously extracted features but also further\r\nenhances the modelâ€™s expressive power and ability to han\x02dle complex scenarios through cross-channel information\r\nfusion.\r\nIn summary, the CrossDySnakeConv module achieves ef\x02ficient feature extraction and fusion by incorporating the\r\nmulti-layer structure of BottleneckDySnakeConv. This module\r\ncaptures multi-level features from input data and fuses features\r\nFig. 5.
